Important News

Wang Jingwei Reports on Diplomacy and Internal Affairs 99

Shanghai Ceasefire Conference Awaits League of Nations Instructions to Proceed

A Detailed and Eloquent Account of the National Crisis Conference

And a Vigorous Rebuttal of Those Dissatisfied with Tutelage

Because Without the Kuomintang, There Would Be No Republic of China

Kuomintang Central Standing Committee member Wang Jingwei delivered the following major report at the morning memorial week meeting on the 25th: "The events of this week that can be reported concern diplomacy and politics. On the diplomatic front, although the Shanghai ceasefire conference has stalled, it has not broken down. We are now waiting for the League of Nations Special Committee to reach a resolution before considering further action. As for the League of Nations investigation team, it has now arrived in the Northeast. Previously, the Manchurian puppet government refused to allow our country's representative to enter the Northeast, but now our country's representative, acting on government instructions, has arrived in the Northeast with the investigation team. They have now begun their investigation and plan to send their first report to the League of Nations around May 1st. On the political front, I would like to report on a few points today. First, the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee resolved to establish people's representative organs at all levels. The Central Political Council resolved to submit this to the Executive Yuan for deliberation and handling. The Executive Yuan has therefore held several meetings. Last Saturday, it held a detailed discussion and reached a general resolution. Originally, there were several types of people's representative organs at the city, county, and provincial levels. Now, it has been decided to start with the city-level people's representative organs. A draft has been prepared, and after further meetings and slight revisions this week, it can be passed and sent to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The draft does not focus on the articles themselves, but on determining the procedures for preparation. It is proposed to start in May, with a three-month period to complete several important tasks of municipal autonomy. Then, within two months, a municipal council will be convened. Cities are now divided into three types: those directly under the National Government, such as Nanjing, Shanghai, Beiping, and Qingdao; ordinary cities, such as Guangzhou; and cities that have been named but not established. They are all relatively easy to concentrate in various parts of the country, so local autonomy will start with the cities, which will be easier to implement. In the future, after the Executive Yuan approves the draft, it will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan and published for the attention and discussion of comrades and all sectors of society. Second, regarding the National Crisis Conference, there were three proposals at the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee in December last year: the National Crisis Conference, the National Salvation Association, and the National Representative Assembly. At that time, it was decided to convene the National Crisis Conference and to limit its discussion to the three areas of resisting aggression, pacifying the country, and providing relief. The National Salvation Association and the National Representative Assembly were submitted to the Central Standing Committee for deliberation. The members of the National Crisis Conference were appointed by the government, while the members of the National Salvation Association and the National Representative Assembly were elected by the people. Their natures were different, and their powers were also different. Before the National Crisis Conference convened, several members requested that political issues be discussed in addition to the three areas of resisting aggression, disaster relief, and pacifying the country. I replied that the scope of the National Crisis Conference was determined by the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee and submitted by the National Government to the Executive Yuan. Although issues outside these three areas could be freely discussed, the Executive Yuan had no power to respond. However, the members from Beiping and Shanghai spoke of the government restricting the scope of discussion. I believed that the facts were present and that there was no need to respond. Later, the National Crisis Conference convened in Luoyang. In addition to the issues of resisting aggression, disaster relief, and pacifying the country, there were also political proposals, especially regarding the issues of tutelage and constitutional government, with various opinions. Taking the two extremes, one was to end tutelage immediately and implement constitutional government, and before the implementation of constitutional government, to reorganize the nature of the government so that it would not be a government of the Kuomintang ruling the country with the party. The other was that the National Crisis Conference should not discuss the issues of tutelage and constitutional government. These issues should be resolved by the Kuomintang's Fifth National Congress. Between these two extreme opinions, there were many different views. Therefore, the proposal review committee first objectively analyzed and organized the various proposals, listed the same points, and reported them to the public. After a day of heated discussion at the conference, the review committee reported its own subjective judgment. What they supported was: first, to ask the government to end tutelage as scheduled, convene a National Assembly, and draft a constitution; second, before the National Assembly, to convene a National Representative Assembly, whose powers would be to deliberate on budgets and final accounts, domestic and foreign public debts, and important international treaties. This proposal was approved by four-fifths of the members present. This proposal was jointly signed by professors from various universities in Wuhan and Beiping. Some of them were members of the party, and some were not. It can be seen that it did not come from the will of one party. After the proposal was passed, I stated that as the President of the Executive Yuan, I could not guarantee that it would be adopted, and even as a member of the Central Committee, I did not have the power to do so. However, I would definitely bring this proposal to the Central Committee and request that the Central Committee decide to adopt it. Thus, it can be seen that their claim that the presentation of issues outside of the three areas of resisting aggression, disaster relief, and pacifying the country was prohibited is completely unfounded. As for now, they say that the members of the National Crisis Conference are mostly composed of officials and party members. This is even more contrary to the facts. If we look at the list of members of the National Crisis Conference, there are officials and party members, but there are even more people outside the party. Furthermore, in terms of the proposals of the National Crisis Conference, very few belong to party members, and many belong to people outside the party. It can be seen that their slander is unfounded. This time, when Comrade Luo Jialun returned from Beiping, he told me that some people are saying that Wang Jingwei advocates that party members should not be elected at all to the National Representative Assembly. This statement is completely fabricated out of thin air. Not only have I never said this, but since the representatives of the National Representative Assembly are elected by the people, what does it have to do with whether they are party members or not? It can be said that they fabricate rumors out of thin air in every possible way. Last time, the Central Political Council had already designated comrades to draft the draft for popularly elected legislative and supervisory members, and comrades have also been designated to jointly and thoroughly examine the National Salvation Association and the National Representative Assembly. It is likely that there will be results at the meeting this afternoon. I do not know whether it will pass. The above are all factual reports. According to the party constitution, everyone can express their personal opinions as much as possible before various issues are resolved, but after a resolution is reached, it must be followed consistently. This is the basic principle of democratic centralism, and it is what we should implement. Therefore, I have some personal opinions to add. Regarding the issue of tutelage, there are now two arguments. The first is that talking about democratic politics means losing the meaning of tutelage. The second is that talking about democratic politics means that one does not need to talk about tutelage. In my opinion, both of these arguments are wrong. I have said before that we must have self-criticism and self-confidence. The first argument, that talking about democratic politics means losing the meaning of tutelage, means losing self-criticism. The second argument, that talking about democratic politics means that one does not need to talk about tutelage, means losing self-confidence. We know that according to the teachings of the Premier, the most important task of the tutelage period is to cultivate civil rights. Therefore, during the tutelage period, the power of the people is increasing day by day in terms of time and expanding day by day in terms of space. If we think that talking about democratic politics means losing the meaning of tutelage, then we are turning the process of tutelage into a party dictatorship like the Communist Party. This is a complete misunderstanding of the Premier's meaning of tutelage to cultivate civil rights. However, the second argument, that talking about democratic politics means that one does not need to talk about tutelage, is also wrong. Many people outside the party now have this argument. Since the founding of the Republic of China, people outside the party have had this common and consistent proposition. This is to overthrow the Kuomintang. That is why people outside the party united under Yuan Shikai after he became president in the first year of the Republic of China. Why? Because they wanted to overthrow the Kuomintang. Now they all advocate abolishing tutelage. Why do they want to abolish tutelage? It is also to overthrow the Kuomintang. However, the method of overthrowing the Kuomintang in the past was to undermine constitutional government, because the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution at that time were all made by Kuomintang members to restrain Yuan Shikai and consolidate the foundation of the Republic of China. Therefore, to overthrow the Kuomintang, they had to undermine constitutional government. Therefore, in the second year of the Republic of China, they helped Yuan Shikai dissolve the parliament and destroy the constitution. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, they dissolved the parliament again and destroyed the constitution. Their first step was to overthrow the Kuomintang, and the second step was to overthrow the Republic of China, because the Republic of China was created by the Kuomintang. This is the united front of a group of bureaucrats and politicians since the Republic of China. They wanted to overthrow the Kuomintang in the past, and they still want to overthrow the Kuomintang now. However, their slogan in the past was to undermine constitutional government, while their slogan now is to support constitutional government. This is because they want to destroy tutelage in the name of supporting constitutional government. We should recognize this clearly. The Premier devoted himself to the National Revolution for forty years. The laws and constitutions of the past were all made by the Kuomintang. The Kuomintang and the Republic of China have the closest relationship. It can be said that without the Kuomintang, there would be no Republic of China. Just look at the time when the Kuomintang was in exile after the first year of the Republic of China, which was the time when the Republic of China was in turmoil. Now that they want to overthrow the Kuomintang, it is precisely the autumn of crisis for the Republic of China. Without the Kuomintang, the future of tutelage would be unimaginable, and the future of constitutional government would be even more unimaginable. They are now deeply saddened that China still does not have constitutional government, but what is the reason for this? This is because since the founding of the Republic of China, constitutional government has been destroyed by them once, twice, and three times. They also say that the Kuomintang has not done well in recent years, but there are facts that can prove it. In the first year of the Republic of China, the Kuomintang was in Nanjing for only a few months. Was there a full opportunity? From the start of tutelage in the seventeenth or eighteenth year of the Republic of China to the present, there have only been three years. If there were no internal conflicts, it would certainly be possible to do better. However, given the size of China, its vastness, and the complexity of the situation, it is impossible for anyone to completely improve China in one or two years. If we doubt that the path of tutelage is impassable, it is not that we doubt the poor work during the tutelage period, but that we doubt the Premier's advocacy of tutelage. The government has failed to properly assist the people in preparing for autonomy due to various internal conflicts. Therefore, the government has extended tutelage for this reason, which is justified. However, we must not abolish tutelage altogether. Furthermore, why can't we have a National Assembly now? This is because constitutional government has not yet begun. However, the National Representative Assembly is different from the National Assembly. According to the provisions of the Founding Program, the National Representative Assembly can be established before the five branches of government are established. Each county that has completed autonomy can elect one National Representative to participate in the central government. The two words "participate in" are very clear. Therefore, the powers of the National Representative Assembly are different from the powers of the National Assembly. The National Assembly is the highest organ of the state, while the National Representative Assembly is a reflection of democratic forces and an organ of the tutelage period. Many comrades have not yet recognized this point clearly, thinking that the National Representative Assembly is the National Assembly. This is a great oversight. If we understand this point, we can understand the meaning of the National Representative Assembly during the tutelage period. As for the people outside the party, thinking that this would overthrow tutelage, they can be even more enlightened. What I wanted to say today is roughly like this. The first half is a report on the diplomatic and political developments of this week, and the second half is a statement of personal opinions. We hope that during the tutelage period, we will work hard to cultivate civil rights so that tutelage can be completed as soon as possible and constitutional government can begin as soon as possible.

League of Nations Investigation Team Arrives in Dalian from Qinhuangdao 100

When Haiqi Entered Dalian, Japanese Police Conducted Large-Scale Martial Law

Compatriots in the Northeast Eagerly Await the Team to Uphold Justice

On the 21st, the Team Took the South Manchuria Railway Train to Shenyang

A Beiping dispatch reports that the League of Nations investigation team arrived in Qinhuangdao at 10:00 AM on the 20th and then divided into three groups to go to the Northeast. The reporter also boarded the Haiqi warship with our delegation to Dalian. After a day and night in Dalian, I returned to Beiping yesterday. Here is an account of what I saw. The investigation team originally intended to travel by special train on the Beining Railway to investigate on the ground, but Japan refused, so the itinerary was divided into two routes. One route was for the two representatives from the United States and Italy and Secretary-General Haas, who took a special train from Shanhaiguan on the pseudo-Fengshan Railway eastward. The other route was for the chairman of the investigation team, Lytton, our country's representative Gu Weijun, and the two representatives from France and Germany, who took the Haiqi and a Japanese destroyer from Qinhuangdao to Dalian. When the special train arrived in Qinhuangdao at 9:40 AM on the 20th, those who followed the sea route disembarked and boarded the Chinese and Japanese warships. Our Haiqi warship left the port first at 10:25 AM, followed by two Japanese destroyers. After sailing a little further, Lytton went to the observation deck on the deck and chatted with Gu Weijun. At this time, the captain of the Haiqi, Jiang Yusheng, and Bao Yimin, led the entire crew to arrange the rooms and prepare lunch. Lytton stayed in Room 1, and Gu Weijun stayed in Room 2. Around 1:00 PM, the captain led the team members into the restaurant for lunch. After the meal, Lytton took a walk on the entire deck. The weather was clear and calm that day, and the ship sailed very steadily. Lytton did not enter the room until 3:30 PM, feeling slightly unwell and feverish. He was examined by Xie Enzeng, a doctor accompanying our delegation. His temperature was 36 degrees, and he took a small amount of medicine and went to bed. At that time, he personally drafted a telegram to the head of the Japanese civil administration office in Dalian, which was sent by the Haiqi. The general idea was that he felt slightly unwell on the way and would stay on the ship when he arrived in Dalian at night. He asked not to be bothered with hospitality and asked to reply by telegram if it was necessary to disembark. At 7:00 PM, the ship passed Laotie Mountain for dinner, but Lytton did not get up. At 11:00 PM, the ship entered the port of Dalian and docked at Pier 2. Japanese police conducted large-scale martial law, and our Haiqi sailors also armed and boarded the deck to prepare. At that time, dozens of people, including the representatives of Honjo Shigeru and Uchida Kosai, and the head of the Dalian civil administration office, had arrived at the pier to welcome them in advance. In addition, there were more than a dozen Chinese traitors and hooligans who followed them onto the ship and demanded to meet with Lytton. Lytton had already gone to bed, so his interpreter turned them away. At this time, more than a dozen Japanese reporters, all wearing white armbands with the words "News Reporter" written on them, surrounded Gu Weijun and talked to him. That night, except for Chen Liting and Yan Enyou from our delegation and Wu Xiufeng and Piert, secretaries of the investigation team, who stayed at the Yamato Hotel, the rest stayed on the ship. At 7:00 AM on the 21st, the reporter and several members of the delegation went ashore to sightsee. As soon as they disembarked, dozens of our compatriots from the Northeast came to inquire whether the investigation team could uphold justice and recounted the suffering of the people in the Northeast. Not many steps out of the pier, a Japanese man in a suit asked us where we were going. We told him that we were just sightseeing. The Japanese man said that this place was far from the lively streets and that we might not know the way, so he asked us to follow him as a guide. We realized that he intended to monitor us and did not want to argue with him, so we hired a car and followed his guidance. We went through Yamagata-dori to Naniwa-cho and went around once. The Japanese man told us that the names of the main streets of Dalian were taken from the names of Japanese military officers who died in the Russo-Japanese War. We asked him where to buy newspapers, and he led us to the Manchuria Newspaper Office, where we bought several newspapers and returned to the ship. That day, the newspaper used large characters to publish that the pseudo-state intended to use force to prevent Gu Weijun from entering the country and, if necessary, would detain Gu in Pulan District. Someone showed the newspaper to Gu, who ignored it. At 9:00 AM, the Japanese representative Yoshida led Claudel and Hini to the Haiqi to meet with Lytton and Gu Weijun. At this time, Lytton's health had improved slightly. After talking for a short time, Yoshida and others left. At 11:00 AM, the special train on the South Manchuria Railway was ready, and the luggage of the team members was transported to the station by footmen. At 11:20 AM, Lytton and Gu Weijun left the cabin. The captain of the Haiqi presented Lytton with a bouquet of flowers. At 12:30 PM, Yoshida and the representatives from Germany and France arrived at the station. Lytton, Gu Weijun, and the other members of our delegation disembarked and took cars prepared by the Japanese police to the station to take the train north. After the investigation team left the ship, the martial law at the pier was lifted. (24th)

Japanese Newspapers Publicize that Britain 101

Tacitly Acknowledges the Manchurian Pseudo-State

Because the Pseudo-State Agrees to Repay British Loans

The Tokyo Jiji Shinpo reported from its Shenyang correspondent that during the Zhang Xueliang era, due to financial chaos, the interest on the British loans for the Fengshan Railway (i.e., the Shenyang-Shanhaiguan section) was in arrears by several million yuan. Now, in order to achieve smooth foreign relations, the Manchurian state is first reorganizing foreign debt. The Fengtian Provincial Government is currently investigating the amount of unpaid interest on the Fengshan Railway and has ordered the director of the Fengshan Railway Bureau to agree on a payment method for principal and interest with the representative of the British Chinese Corporation, the loan country of the Fengshan Railway. It is scheduled to repay 500,000 yuan per month starting in February and will pay off 1 million yuan for February and March in full by the official silver house and the Border Industry Bank. The British loan group is quite satisfied and views the agreement as tacit British recognition of the establishment of the Manchurian state.

Singapore Vigorously Suppresses Japanese Goods 102

Japanese Commerce Suffers a Great Blow

The Kobe Nichika Shinpo reports that Singapore was originally a distribution center for products from Southeast Asia. Three years ago, after the dissolution of the Japanese Industrial Association, the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce and the Indian Chamber of Commerce and Industry occupied a major force in the area. After the Manchurian Incident broke out, the anti-Japanese movement spread to the area. The Japanese residents repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, asking for appropriate countermeasures. The Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry was established in the area and requested recognition from the British colonial authorities. However, since its establishment, wartime disaster insurance has not been underwritten by domestic (Japanese) companies, and the recent rejection of Japanese goods has been particularly fierce. Therefore, our country's commerce has suffered a great blow.

Japanese Goods Imported into China Suddenly Increase 103

Especially Large Imports of Cotton Products and Sugar

The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun reports that the number of our country's goods sent to the interior of China via Qingdao has increased sharply. According to a telegram from the commercial official in Yokohama, the Chinese authorities have recently taken severe measures to crack down on anti-Japanese activities, so Bang Shang (Japanese merchants) have restored their original state in China. Japanese goods that were previously sold to Henan, Shanxi, Jiangsu, Hebei, and Gansu provinces via Tianjin, Hankou, and Shanghai are now being negotiated in Qingdao. The allocation of ships is very active. Among them, cotton products are in the spring demand period, and there are already reservations for goods up to August and September. Since March 1, as many as 15,000 boxes of goods have been imported, and 150,000 catties of refined sugar and red sugar have been imported, which is the largest import in the past years.

Wu Zhongxin's Policy for Governing Anhui 104

Anqing dispatch, Anhui Provincial Government Chairman Wu Zhongxin has already taken office a few days ago. Wu's policy for governing Anhui was not specifically announced at first. At 9:00 AM on the 25th, the new provincial government held its first memorial week, and Wu reported four points of his opinions on provincial affairs: (1) Suppressing bandits: Bandits and communists are rampant in Anhui Province. To make the people live and work in peace, we must first stabilize the locality. Although Chief Commander Chen is in charge of the suppression of bandits, the provincial government must do its best to assist. The first step is to effectively reorganize the defense corps of each county. (2) Disaster relief: After the floods last autumn, the land was barren for thousands of miles, and there were people without food, clothing, and shelter everywhere. Every time I think of their pain, I can't help but feel sad. In the future, I will request the National Government's Disaster Relief Committee to implement good methods to benefit the victims. (3) Reorganizing finance: Anhui's finances are extremely depleted. The committee members waited in Anhui for several days before taking over the job, also because there was no way to raise funds. However, it is difficult to start with revenue generation for a while, so we can only start with cost reduction and reduce administrative expenses as much as possible. (4) Cleaning up the administration: Starting with the various departments and offices of the provincial government, but the clerks will still seek to expand. The quality of officials is closely related to the interests of the locality. In the future, the county magistrates of each county must be selected from those who can be honest and have courage. If they are corrupt and pervert the law, they will be severely punished and will not be tolerated. Other measures that are beneficial to the people will also be implemented in order of urgency. (April 26)

Local News 105

Selling Flower Bridge: Robbery and Assault (Songjiang Correspondence) At Selling Flower Bridge, about ten miles from the northern outskirts of Songjiang, there is a dry goods store opened by Shen Longguan. It has been robbed several times in recent years. Unexpectedly, last night (the 26th), around twelve o'clock, amidst a torrential downpour, more than ten robbers, each wielding pistols and sharp blades, tricked their way into opening the main gate. They forced the owner to hand over his hidden silver. Shen Longguan claimed that it was just a small village shop with meager business. The robbers immediately fired a shot, hitting his right leg, and stabbed him three times. Bleeding profusely, he collapsed to the ground, allowing the robbers to ransack the place and leave triumphantly. Upon inspection, the losses included clothing, jewelry, and about two hundred yuan in cash. The injured owner was carried to the Joseph Hospital for treatment, but his leg bone was broken and had to be amputated. He was then referred to Shanghai Baolong Hospital for radical treatment.

Japanese Plane Crashes and Burns (Taicang Correspondence) Yesterday morning at 9:35 AM, Japanese plane No. 40, which had been flying over Taicang's Great North Gate for reconnaissance, returned at 2:50 PM. After circling the city once, it flew eastward. Unexpectedly, when it reached Xuejiatan, about six miles outside the East Gate of Taicang, the plane suddenly caught fire, emitting thick smoke, and then crashed. The entire plane was destroyed in an instant. The Japanese pilot and two Japanese soldiers were also killed in the crash.

Breakthrough in the Fenshuidun Armory Robbery Case, Key Suspect Arrested (Fengxian Correspondence) Ding Zhiyan, the head of the county police force, received intelligence that Wang Yinchang, the ringleader of the robbery of firearms from the Fenshuidun Public Security Station, was hiding near Dongxin Market in the Fourth District. He immediately acted discreetly and secretly dispatched Special Agent Chief Liu Baoshan, disguised, to capture the suspect. The suspect was apprehended and has already been transferred to the county government. He confessed to the joint robbery. However, the firearms (one Mauser rifle and two other rifles) had already been borrowed by the fugitive Xi Tou Er. The Haiyan Society Case Temporarily Concluded (Wuxi Correspondence) Huang Zhefu, a special commissioner from the Central Party Headquarters, reported that the Wuxi Haiyan Literary Society was suspected of being reactionary. The Wuxi Garrison Command arrested thirteen people, including Wu Wenshan, and sent them to Beijing for interrogation. The Wuxi National Crisis Relief Association argued that those arrested were mostly young male and female students whose ideas might not be entirely orthodox, but whose intentions were not reactionary. They telegraphed Commander Gu of the Garrison Command, requesting a careful interrogation to avoid implicating innocent people. At the same time, fellow villagers in Beijing also worked to clear their names. Commander Gu conducted a thorough interrogation and determined that only Wu Wenshan, Sun Zuyu, Shi Zhaozhou, Hua Yizeng, and Tao Fanggu were more seriously implicated and needed to remain in Beijing for further questioning. The rest were ordered to have their families come to Beijing to provide guarantees and take them back into custody.

Petition to Waive Additional Rent Collection (Wuxi Correspondence) The county government previously received a provincial order to collect two months' rent. At that time, the war in Shanghai was urgent, and local military needs were dire. The county government convened a temporary meeting with various organizations and decided to follow the precedent of 1927, initially collecting one month's rent from urban shops with monthly rents above five yuan, specifically for local emergency needs. The National Crisis Relief Association and the Chamber of Commerce jointly urged the business community to cooperate, which barely managed to achieve the goal. The collected amount was less than 40,000 yuan. Recently, the county government received another telegram from the province, strictly ordering a change to the original plan, with the county Public Security Bureau investigating and collecting from all shops and households, starting from two yuan, for another month. The county government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to begin investigations. Merchants and residents feel that in the current climate of economic depression, having just paid one month's rent, another round of collection would be beyond their means, leading to widespread opposition. Yesterday, the National Crisis Relief Association submitted a petition to the county government, stating the people's hardship and earnestly requesting a waiver.

Business Community Expresses Views on Business Tax (Nantong Correspondence) The Nantong business community, concerned about the self-collection of business tax by the tax bureau this year, convened a general meeting of members through the Chamber of Commerce and resolved on six measures: (1) Petitioning party and government agencies to negotiate with the business tax bureau for a delay in investigation; (2) Self-investigation by the Chamber of Commerce; (3) Correcting last year's approach, with all guilds paying the amounts already determined; (4) Publicly electing representatives to present the business difficulties of the county to the bureau, requesting continued reduction and payment by the Chamber of Commerce; (5) Requesting representatives to notify the provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce to advocate for a unified position among all counties; (6) Unanimously refusing investigation until a resolution is reached.

County Head and Public Security Chief Suddenly Leave Changshu Again (Changshu Correspondence) Tan Yigui, the county head of this county, previously went to the province a week ago to resign due to difficult issues, but returned without success. Yesterday (the 24th), Tan suddenly handed over the official seal to Jin Minjun, the head of the First Section, and Yin Peng, the head of the Public Security Bureau, also handed over the seal to Inspector Lu Baozhong, instructing him to forward it to Section Chief Pan. The two chiefs then left Changshu together in their own gasoline boat at 3:00 PM, leading to many rumors in the outside world.

Strictly Prevent Traitors from Spreading Poison (Gaoyou Correspondence) The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs telegraphed the county government of this county on behalf of Ma Ri, stating that the Public Security Bureau of Funing Town reported the following: Several traitors were recently captured and confessed that they were instructed by the Japanese to spread poison in wells near the locations where Chinese troops were stationed, in order to harm them. Therefore, strict prevention should be ordered.

Water Police Captain Arrested (Gaoyou Correspondence) Gao Zhongkui, the captain of the 25th Squad of the 6th District of the Provincial Water Police Force stationed in Xinghua, has been detained by the Yangzhou Pacification Commissioner's Office for a case. Yesterday, Inspector Zhang telegraphed the county government of this county, ordering the summoning of Teng Yunrong, the town head of Sanduo Town, and Ju Wenfu, a villager of Donghui Town, for questioning.

Zheduo Town Robbed by Bandits (Gaoyou Correspondence) In Zheduo Town, which belongs to the 6th District of the county, more than twenty bandits in uniform suddenly appeared at dusk the day before yesterday. Each wielding firearms, they searched houses one by one and shot and wounded a farmer named Liu San. Furthermore, according to a visitor from Yancheng, Liu Wenkui, the bandit leader who occupied Zheduo Town last autumn, was captured in Yancheng on the 12th of this month and has already been executed.

The 7th Division Comes to Hefei to Assist in Suppressing Communist Bandits (Hefei Correspondence) The central government, due to the rampant banditry of the Six Counties, has decided to launch a large-scale encirclement and suppression to eliminate them. In addition to ordering the Henan-Anhui-Hubei Border Area Pacification Commissioner's Office to dispatch troops stationed in Shangcheng and Gushi to attack the bandits' flanks, it has also ordered the 7th Division under Wang Jun, stationed in Xuzhou and southern Suzhou, to go to Lu'an via Hefei to assist the 55th and 46th Divisions in attacking from the front. Li Shiding, the deputy commander of the 7th Division, led the vanguard 40th Regiment under Du Run and arrived in Dingyuan on the 17th. He dispatched staff officer Lu Xiaozhuang and adjutant Huang Tongyin to Hefei to find the Yibin Building as the divisional headquarters and the garrison locations for various units.

Commissioner Dispatched to Thoroughly Investigate Major Bribery Case (Xiaoshan Correspondence) Lai Jigeng, a resident of Xiangqi Fang in western Xiaoshan, was found to have stored opium, gambling tools, and military weapons at home. The county Public Security Bureau discovered this and dispatched an armed police brigade to search his home a few days ago. As a result, twelve catties of opium, several sets of gambling tiles, and a pistol were found. The witnesses were taken to the county for interrogation. Subsequently, someone came forward to mediate and offered 3,000 yuan as a bribe, which was to be distributed among the Public Security Bureau, the Party Headquarters, and the newspaper. The case has been reported to the provincial government and the Department of Civil Affairs by the other party. Yesterday, the province dispatched Commissioner Wu to rush to Xiaoshan to investigate the facts of the case for verification.

Local News

Chaozhou Fellow Villagers Association Sends Telegram to Zhang Ruigui 106

The banditry in the Nanshan area, bordering the three counties of Chaozhou, Puning, and Huilai in Guangdong, has been cleared since Zhang Ruigui personally led troops to suppress them last month. Post-war work is underway. Yesterday, the Chaozhou Association in Shanghai sent a special telegram to Zhang, which stated: "To Commander Zhang Ruigui of Shantou, We have heard from afar that your troops have suppressed bandits and eliminated harm for the people. We are deeply grateful. We earnestly request that you strictly order your subordinates to be cautious and verify carefully when capturing bandits, and not to implicate innocent people. Also, do not use the search for fugitive bandits as an excuse to extort money from the villagers. Medina Wins This Year's International High-Level Shooting Competition 107

Two Thousand Points to One Thousand Four Hundred and Ninety-Six Points

—Li Gongying First Place with Largest Single Score—

The Shanghai International High-Level Shooting Competition, which has seen fierce competition among heroes for a month, concluded with the Portuguese Medina defeating Li Gongying in the final match yesterday and the day before with a score of 2,000 points to 1,496 points, winning this year's championship. After the competition ended at 11:30 PM last night, Mr. Bu Tuo, the chairman of the Shanghai Amateur Shooting Association, who presided over the competition, reported the results, congratulated Medina on his success, and encouraged Li Gongying to work hard and hope to compete again next year. Then, his wife presented the awards. Medina received the championship silver cup, and Li Gongying received the prize for the largest individual score (143 points in one round). Amid cheers and applause, the closing ceremony was announced.

Yesterday's Championship Process 108

The final was held over two days. On the first day, Medina scored 1,000 points and Li Gongying scored 750 points. Yesterday, the competition continued, with Medina scoring 500 points to 366 points in the first round and 500 points to 380 points in the second round, giving Medina the upper hand in both rounds. In total, Medina scored 2,000 points over the two days, while Li Gongying scored 1,496 points.

Round One: Initially, the two were neck and neck, with little difference in score. However, around the 15th shot, Medina was able to take advantage of every opportunity and score 50 points with one hand, making the situation tense. Li did not show weakness and performed two excellent shots in a row, earning applause from the audience and scoring 63 points, creating a refreshing atmosphere. But after a while, Li remained the same, still unable to stand out, due to not making good use of opportunities, which instead created opportunities for the opponent. After Medina scored large numbers of 54, 67, and 82, the distance between the two widened again, and Medina won the round with 500 points to 366 points.

Round Two: At this time, the scores of the two were nearly 400 points apart. Within ten shots, Medina added more than 100 points, increasing the difference to more than 515 points. Then, he suddenly stopped making progress, with no points scored for seven consecutive shots. Li seized this good opportunity and steadily advanced, at one point bringing the score to 1432 to 1816, reducing the difference to 384 points. But good times don't last forever. Medina showed no mercy and scored again, ultimately winning the final victory with 2,000 points to 1,496 points.

Overview of the Two Players' Skills 109

Li Gongying defeated Medina in 1930, but Medina defeated Li in the following year. Medina's victory again this year means that in recent years, no one in the Shanghai Chinese and Western shooting circles can match the reputation of these two. Even in the future, it may not be easy to cultivate such special talent in the near future, because it is limited to innate qualities. The four games of victories and defeats between the two have been described in detail above, and the fighting skills of the two days are described as follows:

Medina: Short and stout, without pretension, gentle and elegant, with the demeanor of a Confucian general. He can hit the target at will. He is good at flanking warfare. He is especially calm when facing a formidable enemy. His final victory depends on this. Li Gongying: Tall and strong, with robust muscles. Outsiders cannot criticize our country as a sick man. He is good at long-range and close-range shots and is also skilled at deflecting shots. His usual performance is very impressive, but he seems to be inferior in important competitions. This is because his composure is insufficient, and when bad luck comes, he can only sigh and give up.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Allocates Cotton Seeds 112

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in response to the storm damage last year, which harmed crops, believed that the supply of cotton seeds this spring would be insufficient. In November last year, it presented a request to the Municipal Government to allocate funds to purchase hundreds of loads of high-quality cotton seeds from Changshu, Wangyin, and other places, preparing to resell them to farmers in various districts at the original price this spring for planting. Later, due to the outbreak of the Sino-Japanese War, farmers in the entire city were affected by the war and faced livelihood difficulties, urgently needing relief. The bureau, in light of this, presented a request to the Municipal Government a few days ago to allocate the cotton seeds for spring relief, which was approved. The district municipal commissioners and farmers' associations have been ordered to receive and distribute them to provide relief and benefit spring plowing.

The Social Affairs Bureau Rectifies the Rice Export Registration Method 113

In order to prevent the export of rice from aiding the enemy or being transported abroad, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has revised the method of applying for registration and has implemented it. The previous report has been noted. It is heard that the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office also sent an official letter to the bureau, requesting joint restrictions to protect the food supply for the citizens of this city. In addition to sending the revised method to the office, the bureau also strictly handles the new method for those who hold licenses and apply for registration and sealing at various places. If the local government issuing the passport has not directly consulted the bureau in advance with an official letter, they must provide proof documents from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Rice and Grain Guild, or a certified public accountant. Personal guarantees are not allowed. The revised articles of the Rice Export Application Registration Method of the bureau are recorded as follows: (1) The applicant must have a rice procurement passport from the local government of the destination. (2) The applicant must first send the aforementioned passport to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office for sealing. (3) If the local government issuing the passport has not directly consulted this bureau in advance with an official letter, the applicant must provide proof documents from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Rice and Grain Guild, or a certified public accountant, proving that the rice is indeed being transported to the destination stated on the passport. (4) The applicant must fill out the "Rice Export Application Registration Form" according to the format. (5) Those who have fully prepared the aforementioned procedures will be approved by this bureau, registered, and sealed.

The Anti-Opium Society Questions Zhang Xueliang 115

Regarding the Public Sale of Opium in North China

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, due to recent reports in newspapers that the military authorities in the provinces of Hebei, Chahar, and Suiyuan in North China have decided to implement the public sale of opium due to a lack of military funds, specially telegraphed Zhang Xueliang, the Pacification Director of Hebei, yesterday and requested a swift cancellation to ease public grievances. The telegram is recorded as follows: "Urgent. To Mr. Zhang Hanqing, Pacification Director of Beiping. It is reported that, according to recent reports in various newspapers here, the military authorities under your jurisdiction have decided to implement the public sale of opium due to a lack of military funds. The method is to set up a public sale office in each of the provinces of Rehe, Suiyuan, and Hebei, with Gao Jiyi in charge, expecting to obtain two million yuan per month. According to yesterday's report, the public sale of opium in Hebei, Chahar, and Suiyuan is scheduled to be implemented on May 1st. Rehe Province will levy an exit tax. The amount of raw opium arriving in Tianjin has reached more than 3,000 tons, and it is said that 30 million yuan can be collected annually. The exposure of this news has shocked the people of the country, and public opinion is in uproar. The members of our association are particularly alarmed. The central government once brazenly implemented the public sale of opium, but was ultimately opposed by the whole country, and public grievances were rampant. The Executive Yuan then explicitly ordered its cancellation and reiterated the ban on opium. When you were in charge of the outside of the passes, you also vigorously implemented the ban on opium, clearing away those with aspirations, and your reputation spread far and wide. Since the September 18th Incident, however, you have led heavy troops and stationed yourself inside the passes. The voice of criticism from the people of the country has been constant, but you have been understanding, perhaps due to a temporary miscalculation. Now, you are actually picking up the rejected policy of the central government, implementing public sales, poisoning the people, treating laws and regulations as trifles, and destroying public opinion. This kind of measure, even if it can maintain your subordinates and troops for a time, will leave a huge disaster for the nation for generations to come. The disaster of national subjugation and ethnic extermination may not be different from your idea of ​​making money through poisoning. Everyone makes mistakes, but persistent evil leads to doom. If you get on the wrong track, knowing the right way will save you. We guess that you are doing this because the four provinces outside the passes were lost in an instant, ten years of essence was used to aid the enemy, and finances became exhausted. In order to preserve private strength, you are unwilling to reduce expenses. Therefore, you are drinking poison to quench your thirst and are willing to set fire to yourself. You will see that the public will be angry and relatives will be alienated, and even if you have a million brave soldiers, it will be difficult to resist the sanctions of public opinion. What is the use of deploying troops when they cannot be used? How can one raise soldiers to harm the people? If you can lead troops to resist foreign aggression and serve as a national defense, the people will be your backing, and there will be no lack of military expenses. Our association is responsible for rejecting drugs, and we will give our lives for it. For several years, we have admired your clear reputation, but unexpectedly, you have been deeply bewitched at this time, surrounded by those around you, and you have adopted this bad strategy. It is really regrettable. We hope that you will examine the benefits and harms, dismiss the flatterers, focus on self-cultivation, and strive to make up for it later. Immediately issue an order to cancel the harsh policy of the public sale of opium and start anew with the people, so that public sentiment and expectations can still be achieved. We offer our loyal advice and await your instructions. Respectfully, The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society."

The Number of Dock Dues Collected 116

The Maritime Customs authorities notified the Public Works Department that the amount of dock dues collected in the three months of this spring was 39,457.65 taels, which the Public Works Department should receive. According to the budget of the Public Works Department this year, the dock dues are listed at 600,000 taels, which is 150,000 taels less than last year. This is because the Public Works Department has redistributed this tax with neighboring areas, and the increasing number of goods unloaded in Pudong has caused the department's revenue to suffer quite a bit. In 1930, the Public Works Department received 748,336 taels, and in 1931, it received 645,488 taels, including 232,702 taels in autumn, 160,898 taels in summer, 162,605 taels in autumn, and 89,283 taels in winter. Due to the war this year, some ships unloaded goods destined for Shanghai in Hong Kong or Japanese ports in February and March, so the income from dock dues has greatly decreased. According to reports, this tax has always been collected by the Customs on behalf of the Public Works Department.

The Municipal Government-Run Qingning Temple-Across River Ferry Resumes Service 117

The Ferry Fee Still Collects Four Copper Coins

The cross-river ferry between Qingning Temple, run by the Municipal Government, and Dinghai Bridge was suspended because the Dinghai Bridge pier was located in a military area and most passengers did not dare to take it for fear of danger. Now that the situation has eased and the ferry can come and go without hindrance, it resumed service on April 26, from 6:00 AM to 6:00 PM every day. The passenger fare remains the same as the original plan approved by the Municipal Government, charging four copper coins per person per trip.

Huang Chujiu's Jadeite Case 124

Three-Tenths Belong to Liu Baogeng

Already Confirmed by Court Judgment

The Shanghai Daily Night Bank and the Great World Amusement Deposit Department went bankrupt and owed more than 3 million in debt after Huang Chujiu's death two years ago. Creditors filed lawsuits one after another. The former Mixed Court appointed accountants Pan Zhaobang and Wu Cheng to liquidate Huang's Gongfa Company's assets and Huang's private property to repay the debt. Subsequently, the accountants found in Huang's private property catalog a piece of jadeite weighing 330 pounds, worth 16,000 yuan, which was handed over to Liu Baogeng, a jade dealer at No. 454 Lafayette Road, to carve. The accountants filed a petition with the Second Special District Court to summon Liu to the court and order him to deposit the jadeite with the court for disposal. Liu then claimed that this jadeite was jointly purchased with Huang on a daily basis, and he had a 30% share and had paid 4,800 yuan. Huang's sons, Xianzhong and Xianyao, included it in their private property, and his own 30% share was lost. Therefore, he hired lawyer Lin Yingqing as his agent, presented evidence, and filed a lawsuit with the Civil Division of the Second Special Court against the two accountants, Pan and Wu, and Huang's two sons, requesting confirmation of his 30% ownership of the jadeite. Judge Qu Zengze repeatedly held court sessions to collect information, declared the debate closed, and ruled that the plaintiff, Liu Baogeng, had a 30% co-ownership of the jadeite, and rejected the lawsuit against Pan Zhaobang and Wu Cheng. The plaintiff bore one-fifth of the litigation costs, and Huang Xianzhong and Xianyao bore four-fifths. The judgment has been served and confirmed.

Midnight Chopping with a Kitchen Knife

Zhang Liang Failed to Become a Lawyer and Went to Jail 135

Forging Diplomas to Make a Living

Investigation Reveals the Arrest

Zhang Liang, courtesy name Chaoren, 29 years old, from Huzhou, lives at No. 2 Fenghuan Lane, Fangxie Road, West Gate. He has a prestigious job in society. He believes that the Shanghai lawyer profession has been thriving in recent years. He was eager to try. He obtained a forged 14th-year graduation diploma from the Zhejiang Public Law School and submitted it to the Lawyer Qualification Committee of the Judicial Yuan to apply for a lawyer's license. Suspecting that the diploma was questionable, the committee sent a letter to the school to inquire whether there was a graduate named Zhang Liang. The school found no such person and reported to the Ministry of Justice, which secretly ordered the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office to arrest him. Zhu Wan, a secret agent, was secretly dispatched to arrest him. It has been more than a month, but Zhang no longer lives there and cannot be arrested. The day before yesterday, the bailiff found his relatives and learned where Zhang was recently living. Fearing that he would be alerted, he wrote a note stating that the certificate had been sent to the court and asked him to go to the court to collect it with a photo for verification. Zhang was overjoyed after receiving the note. He first ordered his brother to take the photo to the court to contact the bailiff. After observing that it was not the person himself, he ordered him to bring the person himself to collect it. Yesterday, Zhang personally went to the court. The bailiff then showed the arrest warrant. Zhang was shocked and repeatedly shouted that he had been tricked. He immediately reported to the prosecutor to open the court. Zhang confessed that the diploma was given by a friend surnamed Wang, who filled in the name, date, and year, and he affixed the stamps himself. He said that he completely wanted to make a living. The official immediately ordered him to be detained for further investigation.

Free Talk

Giro's Words and Deeds 141

— Yi Qiu From Suzhou

Dr. Giro, who travels the globe, is a Caucasian from Turkey's neighboring country. Since joining the Chinese Nationalist Party in 1918, he has been determined to promote the Three People's Principles, awaken small and weak nations, and seek the realization of world harmony. In the spring of the year before last, he entered China and traveled to various places. So far, he has traveled to seventeen provinces. In the past, Dr. Giro and his translator, Mr. Qiao, came to Suzhou from Hangzhou and stayed at the Xinchan Hotel in Jinmen. Many people from all walks of life in this city went to visit him. I admired his great spirit and went to visit him. I was honored to hear his talk, which was quite alarming, and he had many important points on the way to resist Japan. I was inspired by listening to it, so I summarized and recorded it as follows. (The following are all Mr. Ji's words) Japan's annexation of the Northeast was indeed a planned action, but it was also based on the dramatic progress of Chinese people's intelligence. If it was delayed, it would be difficult to start. Therefore, it was launched decisively on September 18. However, China not only did not resist, but also endured humiliation and sought perfection, begging for mercy from the League of Nations, exposing its weaknesses, which led to the Shanghai Incident. However, China was still not aware of it. Millions of troops across the country were only fighting with the Nineteenth Route Army and the Fifth Route Army. Of course, they were outnumbered and not to the point of utter defeat. It was already a great fortune, but the government authorities still relied on the League of Nations and did not seek their own resolution. It is really puzzling. I know deeply that the League of Nations is the main camp of the great powers. Weak countries can never get any help from it. To put it bluntly, seeking the League of Nations is like a lamb in distress, seeking help from jackals and wolves, just to hasten its own demise. The only way for China to save itself now is to awaken the people of the whole country, save money on food and clothing, purchase military fire, and prepare for armed resistance. All the troops in the country should be sent to the border to implement self-defense. The people of the whole country should implement a thorough economic boycott of Japan. After one year, Japan can be paralyzed. After two years, Japan can be destroyed without attack. There is one more thing that deserves special attention. I hope you will tell your compatriots. I passed through Hong Kong and met Mrs. Luren, a White Russian general. According to her, all White Russians are fed by the Japanese. They have now been concentrated in various places, waiting for an opportunity to disrupt China. From this point of view, China is like a lone boat trapped in a storm. There are enemies in front, behind, left, and right. If we do not rise up and plan for it quickly, disaster will be imminent.

The Robbery of Malu 142

— Sun Choucheng

During this Japanese invasion, Jiading County was completely occupied by the enemy. Most of the residents of the county moved to Qingpu. Yesterday, I met an old friend, Mr. Zhang, who talked about the situation of his hometown, Malu, being ravaged by the Japanese army. It was so tragic that it was unbearable to hear. So I picked up a few things to express my grief. (1) Malu is an important road from Nanxiang to Jiading, with about hundreds of households and twenty or thirty shops. After the outbreak of the Shanghai War, the Japanese disguised themselves as villagers and went to the town to investigate military intelligence. They were arrested by the Defense Regiment. After Mr. Zhang's uncle briefly inquired, he was released lightly. Unexpectedly, after the Japanese army occupied the town, the previously arrested Japanese spy falsely accused Mr. Zhang's uncle of being the leader of the plainclothes team. He had been tied to the playground of the central elementary school, preparing to be shot. Fortunately, a gentleman who had worked in a Japanese store in Hongkou had kinship with him, spoke Japanese, and proved that he had opened a pharmacy, was nearly seventy years old, was kind, and believed in Buddhism, and was definitely not the leader of the plainclothes team, so he was spared. (2) An old woman surnamed Wang, a farmer in a village near Malu, was over sixty years old, energetic, and usually led her children and daughters-in-law to engage in agriculture, working diligently. When the Nineteenth Route Army retreated to the second line of defense, the neighboring residents fled far away. She could not bear to abandon the family she had built with her own hands for decades, so she ordered her children and daughters-in-law to flee to other towns, while she stayed in her home to observe the situation. After the Japanese army arrived in the town, they searched everywhere. When they went to her house, they rummaged through boxes and cabinets and plundered away. Before leaving, they saw the old woman pressing her chest with her hand, suspecting that she was hiding military fire. They ordered her to take off her clothes for inspection. The old woman firmly refused, which led to her being shot. Afterwards, her children and daughters-in-law returned home and only saw bloodstains. They did not see the body. They still hoped that she would return alive. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, they were digging a ditch with hoes and found a leg. They removed the mud and saw the whole body. According to them, she refused to be searched because she had banknotes hidden on her body. After being shot, the Japanese soldiers looted everything and abandoned the body in the field.

World Short Notes 143

— Hai Ke

The Light World of Fish There are several seas and oceans in the world, the depth of which is fully five miles. Below is pitch black, and any light cannot reach. Therefore, the water pressure is extremely strong. Even in that dark water depth, there are many strange fish living there, which will never collide, because nature gives them a light, each shining on their heads, which can illuminate the way of travel without hindrance. The kind of light is very strange. It turns out that there are several kinds of microorganisms that can emit phosphorescence. Thousands of them live together, forming a bright colony. They often live in the middle of the fish scales, and when you look at them, it is a bright light. Some fish open their own power plants, because their scales will glow by themselves without the help of microorganisms. There are also many fish on the seabed that have two eyes mounted on long, fleshy stalks that protrude in front and can also be used as bright lights. Even more strangely, some fish grow a fleshy stalk in their nose, and a small lamp is installed on the head of the stalk, just above its large lower jawbone. When small fish see the light, they swim up to watch and play and are swallowed into their stomachs.

Record of a Two-Sided Military Career (37) 145

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter 5: The ungrateful termination of friendship unfortunately provokes the anger of a generous stranger. The most difficult thing to bear is the kindness of a beautiful woman.

After the incident, Anjia Village was burned and killed, and nine out of ten houses were empty. Only corpses and rubble remained on the ground. Niu Heifeng finally vented his anger and led the bandits away. When the officers and soldiers heard the news and came to rescue, Niu Heifeng had already gone far away, and the sacrifice of Anjia Village was in vain. Seeing that he had caused a great disaster, An Dakui was so frightened that he fled the bandit area overnight and returned to the military headquarters to work. Fortunately, his family had already been taken outside, so he was unharmed. Now he occupied the property of a firm, so he did not even recognize his own nephew. Looking at it, this person was so greedy that he was not good enough to his family or friends. When Wei Zhuomou talked about this with indignation, he could not help but temporarily put away his joking attitude and issued extremely radical remarks, advising An Yutian to tell his fellow villagers and unite to bring him to justice. An Yutian was sobbing and sighing. At this point, he suddenly sighed and said, "What Uncle Dakui did is certainly not right, but Niu Heifeng is an evil bandit, and I have a deadly feud with him. I cannot take revenge on outsiders first, but only know to settle accounts and fight for property with my family. It is still not right. Let's forget it. Now I am determined not to let him provide me with expenses. Is the world so big that I, An Yutian, with a seven-foot body, cannot be self-reliant and make a living?" Wei Zhuomou immediately laughed and said, "Good. You really have ambition. I admire you." As he said this, he glanced at Liang Xiaoyun. He only saw that she always maintained a humorous state and did not praise him rashly, but turned her beautiful eyes to Wei Zhuomou's side, as if to say that she wanted to say something, but it was inconvenient to say it while you were here. Wei Zhuomou understood and got up to say goodbye, "I have said everything I should report. I can't be so ignorant and stay here to be an annoying person. I'd better roll first before the duck egg grows feet, so that you two can talk quietly for a while." After saying that, he ran away with a book, grinning and shaking his head. Liang Xiaoyun did not retain him, but remained very calm and sat opposite An Yutian in the study. An Yutian only lowered his head and sighed, and had nothing else to say to Liang Xiaoyun. After a while, Liang Xiaoyun stretched lazily. That delicate and languid sigh startled An Yutian and made him look up at her. He happened to meet Liang Xiaoyun's charming and soft eyes. An Yutian just felt dazed, but Liang Xiaoyun's cheeks were also slightly red, and she said with a smile, "I'm a little tired. Why don't you accompany me to the other room? Let's lie down for a while and talk. How about it?"

Finance 146

The Price of Silver Sycee Continues to Fall Endlessly?

Breaking Through the 7 Qian Mark

Inventory Exceeds 20.6 Million

Source Continues to Flow In Abundantly

Market Overview: Since the dramatic changes brought about by the invasion of Shanghai by the violent Japanese, the city's commerce has undergone repeated transformations. The financial sector, as the linchpin of all industries, could hardly maintain stability on its own. This time, it has been overwhelmed by the influx of sources from various ports, while sales have stagnated, leading to a remarkably large inventory. According to recent surveys, it has already exceeded 20.6 million, truly a new record. Moreover, the inflow of sources from various ports along the Yangtze River continues unabated, amounting to hundreds of thousands or one to two million each day, leaving the price of silver sycee unable to resist, resulting in a catastrophic decline with no end in sight.

Sycee Exchange Rates: "Foreign Sycee" fell close to the 7 qian mark yesterday morning, reaching 6 qian, 9 fen, 9 li and a half, lower by 7 hao and a half compared to the lowest price in the previous day's afternoon market. In the afternoon market, the general sentiment was that such a low price could not compete, but no one dared to buy in speculatively, so transactions were few. The price remained the same as in the morning market, at 6 qian, 9 fen, 9 li and a half. "Silver Sycee" remained at 1 qian in both the morning and afternoon markets, with banks quoting 4 fen. However, the practice of adding water to the drawings seemed to have become excessively lax, with blank drawings being offered yesterday, but no one accepting them, mainly due to the excessive padding. However, this market price fluctuates unpredictably, making it difficult to set a reliable benchmark for the market.

Subsidiary Coin Market Conditions: Jiangnan small silver dollars followed the fall of foreign silver sycee, dropping to 6 qian with nothing extra in the morning and afternoon markets, down 1 li and 7 hao and a half from the previous day's morning market. Transactions were 2,000 jiao in the morning market and 1,500 jiao in the afternoon market. Guangdong small silver dollars also fell due to the drop in foreign silver sycee, in order to maintain a balanced exchange rate, falling close to the 6 qian mark yesterday, reaching 5 qian, 9 fen, 8 li in the morning market and 5 qian, 9 fen, 6 li and a half in the afternoon market, a decrease of 5 li and 2 hao and a half compared to the previous day's morning market. Transactions were 155,000 jiao in the morning market and 30,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins rose along with the others by 2,500 wen, reaching 419,500 wen, only a limited distance from the 420,000 wen mark. This is also unprecedented since there was a market price for copper coins.

Silver Dollar Inflow and Outflow: "Silver Funds" were quite active in bank receipts and disbursements yesterday. Chinese merchants took in over 3.2 million in various receipts, foreign merchants over 4.4 million, and exchange, cargo mortgage, customs duties, and advances amounted to slightly over 6 million. Money shops and silver public firms took in over 29 million, silver drawing funds took in over 2.3 million, and exchange ticket transactions also reached over 2.3 million, an increase of several hundred thousand compared to the previous day. "Foreign Funds" exchange ticket funds totaled 840,000 in the morning market and 365,000 in the afternoon market. Banknotes were 70,000 in the morning market and 10,000 in the afternoon market. Interbank trading in the morning market was 750,000 and in the afternoon market 300,000. Various banks' foreign accounts had receipts and disbursements of over 1.1 million, banknote inflows and outflows were 700,000 to 800,000, money shops' foreign public firms had receipts and disbursements of over 4.8 million, re-drawing funds totaled over 1.4 million, and small silver dollar shop transactions amounted to over 500,000.

Forward Gold Advances 147

Soaring to 10 Taels, 9 Qian

Active Buyers: Forward gold rebounded and trended higher, with excellent momentum, advancing the price by as much as four or five taels. There was a total difference of ten taels between the morning and evening sessions, ultimately rising by more than ten taels. The rise was evident from the start, even though the silver market had not changed. Furthermore, repeated sharp declines in exchange rates, with the British exchange secretly stabilizing, and the trend of the U.S. dollar remaining strong, further boosted confidence. Consequently, the price broke through 720 taels. However, a slight pullback at noon brought out sellers, and the market then resumed its upward trend, driven by demand exceeding supply, eventually exceeding 20 taels. The lack of market activity for bills of exchange on Wednesday contributed to the situation.

High Opening: The June contract opened high, adding 2 taels and 7 qian, reaching 712 taels and a half. There were expectations of further gains overnight, but this did not materialize. Although the U.S. dollar increased in price, purchases were not affected, as the private telegraphic rate for silver was down by one-eighth, boosting confidence. Yuan Heng, Heng Yu, Tai Chang, and others took the lead in advancing, adding 3 taels until 9:30 a.m., when HSBC quoted a British gold increase of 1.25 and a U.S. dollar decrease of 1.25, reaching 15 taels and 6 qian. Fluctuations of around one tael occurred within half an hour, reflecting the prices of bank transactions. British gold initially absorbed half a penny, and U.S. dollars for forward settlement reached .375, then .1875. Mitsui bought May at .0625, and HSBC offered August British gold at .375. The buying spree by Yuan Heng, Hong Kang, Yong Fu, Tai Heng, Xie Yu, Yong Tong, Tai Chang, Shun Li, and others drove the price beyond 20 taels, reaching 21 taels after 10 a.m. Zih Feng, Yong Yi Feng, Kang Yuan, Kang Xiang, and others then sold, retreating to 18 taels and a half after twenty-five minutes. Fortunately, the exchange market remained tight. Anda absorbed August U.S. dollars at .1875, and Hua Bank absorbed May at 31 yuan, also hedging British gold at .375. Yuan Chun, Da De Cheng, Wu Pin, Yong Feng, and others showed strong buying interest. Rumor had it that a certain bank had opened 210 spot contracts sold by Tong Feng Yong, but the bank denied it. The market price surged upwards, reaching 22 taels and 5 qian at 10:30 a.m. Afterwards, Yi Feng, Yong Yuan, Da Yong, Zih Feng, Yong Hong Kang, Yong Tong, Tai Chang, and other miscellaneous bulls took the opportunity to sell, causing a sharp drop of over 5 taels, hovering around one tael until 11:30 a.m., reaching 17 taels and 3 qian. Guangdong firms slightly advanced, raising the price by two taels to 19 taels and a half, closing at 17 taels and 7 qian at noon. Wu Pin and others then advanced, adding to more than 18 taels. The quoted price was changed to 787 taels, with a discount of about 70 taels.

Continued Strength in the Afternoon Market: The afternoon market opened higher by 1 tael, reaching 18 taels and 8 qian, then 19 taels, before retreating to 18 taels. With active buyers such as Fu Yu, Yi Feng, Zih Feng, Yong Wu Pin, and others competing to buy, the price gradually increased by four taels, reaching 22 taels at 3:45 p.m., with good momentum. After some short covering, retail sellers slightly lagged by two taels, reaching 20 taels, and closing at 20 taels and 7 qian at 4:30 p.m., briefly reaching 22 taels. This was a head-covering drag-in. Compared to the day before (based on quoted prices), it was up by 10 taels and 9 qian, with a range of 10 taels between the maximum of 22 taels and 5 qian and the minimum of 12 taels and 5 qian throughout the day. The quoted price had a discount of around 65 to 66 taels. The account was 18 taels, with a water supplement of 18 taels in the morning and 21 taels in the afternoon, adding 6 taels to the bare contract.

Numerous New Participants: Transaction statistics on the trading floor showed more buyers than sellers. Yuan Heng, Wan Xing, Xie Xing Yong, Fu Xing Yong, Yuan Cheng Yong, Hong Kang Yong, Fu Tai Heng, Heng Xing, Tong Tai Chang all bought, while Shun Li, Zih Feng Yong, Yi Feng Yong, and head-coverers all sold. Yuan Tai, Yuan Mao Yong, Heng Yu, Yu He, Long Sheng, and others handled a large volume of transactions. In the afternoon, Yi Feng, Zih Feng Yong, Hong Kang Yong, Yi Feng Yong, and Tai Feng Cheng all bought, while Yuan Kang Xiang offset their previous short positions. Yuan Mao Yong and retail sellers all sold.

Cotton Yarn: No Hope for Recovery Under Various Pressures 151

Another Decline of 5 Qian to Over 1 Liang

The cotton yarn market's declining trend has not stopped, and the situation is very weak. Constrained by finance and burdened by last year's severe drought, the situation in the interior is indescribable. Purchasing power has been greatly reduced, and the price of foreign silver sycee has fallen below 7 qian, increasing anxiety. However, Sichuan merchants have made some purchases. According to some sources, business with the outside world in Sichuan is still difficult to improve, and the economic situation is dire, making large transactions difficult to realize. Although the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce is trying to resolve the closure of Guangdong silver shops, it is still difficult to recover in the short term, which has greatly affected yarn sales. As a result, market sentiment remains depressed. Some popular yarns have temporarily stabilized after days of sharp declines, but unpopular yarns continue to fall sharply. Based on the current situation, there is no hope for recovery in the short term.
